## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Cross-Org gRPC Service Definition Discovery

## Your Task

Find the gRPC service definitions that are shared between `envoyproxy/envoy` and `grpc/grpc`. Specifically: 1. In `envoyproxy/data-plane-api`, find all `.proto` files that define `service` declarations using `rpc` methods (the xDS service definitions). 2. In `grpc/grpc`, find the source files that implement the `grpc_health_v1.Health` service (the standard gRPC health checking protocol). Report the repo, file path, and service name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about gRPC services shared between envoyproxy/data-plane-api and grpc/grpc repositories.

### Key Findings:

**From envoyproxy/data-plane-api (31 proto files):**
- **xDS Discovery Services**: CDS, EDS, LDS, RDS, SDS, VHDS, SRDS, LEDS, RTDS, ADS
- **Supporting Services**: CSDS, ALS, MetricsService, LRS, RLS, RLQS, Authorization, ExternalProcessor, HealthDiscoveryService, NetworkExternalProcessor, TapSinkService
- Services available in both v2 and v3 API versions

**From grpc/grpc (1 proto file):**
- **Health Service** (grpc.health.v1.Health) - Standard gRPC health checking protocol
- Implementation files: `src/cpp/server/health/health_check_service.cc` and `src/cpp/server/health/default_health_check_service.cc`

### Answer Format:
The `answer.json` file includes:
- **files**: All 32 proto file paths
- **symbols**: All 35 service definitions with their locations
- **chain**: Implementation references for the gRPC Health service
- **text**: Detailed narrative explaining the services, their organization, and cross-organizational usage

These services form the foundation of the xDS protocol and gRPC infrastructure, enabling communication between data planes (like Envoy) and control planes using a standardized gRPC-based service discovery and health checking protocol.

  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\\\";\\n8: \\n9: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n10: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n11: \\n12: import \\\"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n16: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n17: \\n18: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n19: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExternalProcessorProto\\\";\\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n21: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\\n25: \\n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\\n28: //\\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\";\n8: \n9: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n10: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n11: \n12: import \"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExternalProcessorProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\n25: \n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\n28: //\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. Discovery\\n\\n### Envoy Data Plane API (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)\\n\\nThe data-plane-api repository contains gRPC service definitions for the xDS (service discovery) protocol and supporting Envoy services. These services are organized across multiple proto files and versions (v2, v2alpha, and v3).\\n\\n#### xDS Discovery Services (Core)\\nThese are the primary service discovery services used by Envoy and other xDS clients:\\n\\n1. **ClusterDiscoveryService (CDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/cluster/v3/cds.proto and envoy/api/v2/cds.proto. Provides cluster configuration discovery.\\n\\n2. **EndpointDiscoveryService (EDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/eds.proto and envoy/api/v2/eds.proto. Provides endpoint/load assignment discovery.\\n\\n3. **ListenerDiscoveryService (LDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/listener/v3/lds.proto and envoy/api/v2/lds.proto. Provides listener configuration discovery.\\n\\n4. **RouteDiscoveryService (RDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides route configuration discovery.\\n\\n5. **SecretDiscoveryService (SDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/secret/v3/sds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/sds.proto. Provides secret (TLS certificate) discovery.\\n\\n6. **VirtualHostDiscoveryService (VHDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides virtual host configuration discovery.\\n\\n7. **ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService (SRDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/srds.proto and envoy/api/v2/srds.proto. Provides scoped route configuration discovery.\\n\\n8. **LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService (LEDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/leds.proto. Provides locality-specific endpoint discovery.\\n\\n9. **RuntimeDiscoveryService (RTDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/runtime/v3/rtds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/rtds.proto. Provides runtime configuration discovery.\\n\\n10. **AggregatedDiscoveryService (ADS)** - Defined in envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/ads.proto. Provides multiplexed access to all xDS services.\\n\\n#### Supporting Services\\nThese services provide additional functionality for Envoy:\\n\\n11. **ClientStatusDiscoveryService (CSDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/status/v3/csds.proto and envoy/service/status/v2/csds.proto. Allows clients to report their configuration status to management servers.\\n\\n12. **AccessLogService (ALS)** - Defined in envoy/service/accesslog/v3/als.proto and envoy/service/accesslog/v2/als.proto. Streams access logs to an external logging service.\\n\\n13. **MetricsService** - Defined in envoy/service/metrics/v3/metrics_service.proto and envoy/service/metrics/v2/metrics_service.proto. Streams metrics to an external metrics service.\\n\\n14. **LoadReportingService (LRS)** - Defined in envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto and envoy/service/load_stats/v2/lrs.proto. Reports load statistics to the management server.\\n\\n15. **RateLimitService (RLS)** - Defined in envoy/service/ratelimit/v3/rls.proto and envoy/service/ratelimit/v2/rls.proto. Provides rate limiting decisions.\\n\\n16. **RateLimitQuotaService (RLQS)** - Defined in envoy/service/rate_limit_quota/v3/rlqs.proto. Manages rate limit quota allocations.\\n\\n17. **Authorization** - Defined in envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto. Provides authorization checks for incoming requests.\\n\\n18. **ExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto. Allows external processing of HTTP requests and responses.\\n\\n19. **HealthDiscoveryService (HDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/health/v3/hds.proto. Enables Envoy instances to perform health checks on behalf of the management server.\\n\\n20. **NetworkExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/network_ext_proc/v3/network_external_processor.proto. Provides external processing capabilities for L4 network traffic.\\n\\n21. **TapSinkService** - Defined in envoy/service/tap/v2alpha/tap.proto. Receives captured traffic taps from Envoy.\\n\\n### gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc/grpc)\\n\\nThe gRPC repository includes the standard gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc_health_v1):\\n\\n**Health Service** - Defined in src/proto/grpc/health/v1/health.proto. This is the standard gRPC health checking service that provides two RPC methods:\\n- Check: Performs a one-time health check for a service\\n- Watch: Streams health status changes for a service\\n\\nImplementation files for the Health service in gRPC:\\n- src/cpp/server/health/health_check_service.cc - Core implementation\\n- src/cpp/server/health/default_health_check_service.cc - Default implementation\\n\\n### Cross-Organization Usage\\n\\nThese services represent the interface between Envoy (the data plane) and management servers (xDS providers) using a common gRPC-based protocol. The Health service is used by Envoy and other gRPC services to report their operational status. Together, they form the fundamental building blocks for service mesh control planes and gRPC infrastructure.\\n\"\n}\n",

Discovery\\n\\n### Envoy Data Plane API (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)\\n\\nThe data-plane-api repository contains gRPC service definitions for the xDS (service discovery) protocol and supporting Envoy services. These services are organized across multiple proto files and versions (v2, v2alpha, and v3).\\n\\n#### xDS Discovery Services (Core)\\nThese are the primary service discovery services used by Envoy and other xDS clients:\\n\\n1. **ClusterDiscoveryService (CDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/cluster/v3/cds.proto and envoy/api/v2/cds.proto. Provides cluster configuration discovery.\\n\\n2. **EndpointDiscoveryService (EDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/eds.proto and envoy/api/v2/eds.proto. Provides endpoint/load assignment discovery.\\n\\n3. **ListenerDiscoveryService (LDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/listener/v3/lds.proto and envoy/api/v2/lds.proto. Provides listener configuration discovery.\\n\\n4. **RouteDiscoveryService (RDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides route configuration discovery.\\n\\n5. **SecretDiscoveryService (SDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/secret/v3/sds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/sds.proto. Provides secret (TLS certificate) discovery.\\n\\n6. **VirtualHostDiscoveryService (VHDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides virtual host configuration discovery.\\n\\n7. **ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService (SRDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/srds.proto and envoy/api/v2/srds.proto. Provides scoped route configuration discovery.\\n\\n8. **LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService (LEDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/leds.proto. Provides locality-specific endpoint discovery.\\n\\n9. **RuntimeDiscoveryService (RTDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/runtime/v3/rtds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/rtds.proto. Provides runtime configuration discovery.\\n\\n10. **AggregatedDiscoveryService (ADS)** - Defined in envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/ads.proto. Provides multiplexed access to all xDS services.\\n\\n#### Supporting Services\\nThese services provide additional functionality for Envoy:\\n\\n11. **ClientStatusDiscoveryService (CSDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/status/v3/csds.proto and envoy/service/status/v2/csds.proto. Allows clients to report their configuration status to management servers.\\n\\n12. **AccessLogService (ALS)** - Defined in envoy/service/accesslog/v3/als.proto and envoy/service/accesslog/v2/als.proto. Streams access logs to an external logging service.\\n\\n13. **MetricsService** - Defined in envoy/service/metrics/v3/metrics_service.proto and envoy/service/metrics/v2/metrics_service.proto. Streams metrics to an external metrics service.\\n\\n14. **LoadReportingService (LRS)** - Defined in envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto and envoy/service/load_stats/v2/lrs.proto. Reports load statistics to the management server.\\n\\n15. **RateLimitService (RLS)** - Defined in envoy/service/ratelimit/v3/rls.proto and envoy/service/ratelimit/v2/rls.proto. Provides rate limiting decisions.\\n\\n16. **RateLimitQuotaService (RLQS)** - Defined in envoy/service/rate_limit_quota/v3/rlqs.proto. Manages rate limit quota allocations.\\n\\n17. **Authorization** - Defined in envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto. Provides authorization checks for incoming requests.\\n\\n18. **ExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto. Allows external processing of HTTP requests and responses.\\n\\n19. **HealthDiscoveryService (HDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/health/v3/hds.proto. Enables Envoy instances to perform health checks on behalf of the management server.\\n\\n20. **NetworkExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/network_ext_proc/v3/network_external_processor.proto. Provides external processing capabilities for L4 network traffic.\\n\\n21. **TapSinkService** - Defined in envoy/service/tap/v2alpha/tap.proto. Receives captured traffic taps from Envoy.\\n\\n### gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc/grpc)\\n\\nThe gRPC repository includes the standard gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc_health_v1):\\n\\n**Health Service** - Defined in src/proto/grpc/health/v1/health.proto. This is the standard gRPC health checking service that provides two RPC methods:\\n- Check: Performs a one-time health check for a service\\n- Watch: Streams health status changes for a service\\n\\nImplementation files for the Health service in gRPC:\\n- src/cpp/server/health/health_check_service.cc - Core implementation\\n- src/cpp/server/health/default_health_check_service.cc - Default implementation\\n\\n### Cross-Organization Usage\\n\\nThese services represent the interface between Envoy (the data plane) and management servers (xDS providers) using a common gRPC-based protocol. The Health service is used by Envoy and other gRPC services to report their operational status. Together, they form the fundamental building blocks for service mesh control planes and gRPC infrastructure.\\n\"\n}\n",
